Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output size:\n        - 'valid': output size is ``len(a) - window_size + 1`` (default)\n        - 'same': output size is ``len(a)`` (padded to match input)\n        - 'full': output size is ``len(a) + window_size - 1`` (padded on both sides)\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    out : ndarray\n        A rolling median array. The shape depends on the mode parameter.\n        For 'valid' mode, the output shape is reduced along the specified axis.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer or is larger than the array\n        size in 'valid' mode.\n    TypeError\n        If the input cannot be converted to an array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median of array elements.\n    numpy.convolve : Discrete linear convolution of two one-dimensional sequences.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    across the array and computing the median of each window.\n\n    For arrays with NaN values, the median will follow NumPy's default behavior\n    of including NaN in the calculation.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> from numpy.lib import rolling_median\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asanyarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, int) or window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    # mode == 'full'\n        output_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n\n    # Prepare output array\n    output_shape = list(a.shape)\n    output_shape[axis] = output_size\n    result = np.empty(output_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Flatten all other axes for easier processing\n    orig_shape = a_moved.shape\n    a_flat = a_moved.reshape(a_moved.shape[0], -1)\n    result_flat = result_moved.reshape(result_moved.shape[0], -1)\n\n    # The shape depends on the mode parameter.\n        For 'valid' mode, the output shape is reduced along the specified axis.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If window_size is not a positive integer or is larger than the array\n        size in 'valid' mode.\n    TypeError\n        If the input cannot be converted to an array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median of array elements.\n    numpy.convolve : Discrete linear convolution of two one-dimensional sequences.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    across the array and computing the median of each window.\n\n    For arrays with NaN values, the median will follow NumPy's default behavior\n    of including NaN in the calculation.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> from numpy.lib import rolling_median\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    >>> rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 5. ])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asanyarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, int) or window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if a.ndim == 0:\n        raise ValueError(\"input array must have at least 1 dimension\")\n\n    if axis is None:\n        axis = 0\n    else:\n        axis = axis % a.ndim\n\n    # Get the size of the axis we're working on\n    axis_size = a.shape[axis]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        if window_size > axis_size:\n            raise ValueError(\n                f\"window_size ({window_size}) cannot be larger than the \"\n                f\"array size ({axis_size}) in 'valid' mode\"\n            )\n        output_size = axis_size - window_size + 1\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        output_size = axis_size\n    else:  # mode == 'full'\n        output_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n\n    # Prepare output array\n    output_shape = list(a.shape)\n    output_shape[axis] = output_size\n    result = np.empty(output_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Handle 'same' and 'full' modes by padding\n    if mode == 'same':\n        pad_before = window_size // 2\n        pad_after = window_size - pad_before - 1\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = window_size - 1\n    else:\n        pad_before = 0\n        pad_after = 0\n\n    if pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0:\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n        a_padded = np.pad(a, pad_width, mode='edge')\n    else:\n        a_padded = a\n\n    # Compute rolling median\n    padded_size = a_padded.shape[axis]\n\n    # Move the target axis to position 0 for easier iteration\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a_padded, axis, 0)\n    result_moved = np.moveaxis(result, axis, 0)\n\n    # Flatten all other axes for easier processing\n    orig_shape = a_moved.shape\n    a_flat = a_moved.reshape(a_moved.shape[0], -1)\n    result_flat = result_moved.reshape(result_moved.shape[0], -1)\n\n    # Compute rolling median for each position\n    for i in range(output_size):\n        window_data = a_flat[i:i+window_size, :]\n        # Compute median for each column\n        for j in range(window_data.shape[1]):\n            result_flat[i, j] = np.median(window_data[:, j])\n\n    # Reshape result back to original dimensions\n    result_moved = result_flat.reshape(orig_shape)\n    result = np.moveaxis(result_moved, 0, axis)\n\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":37,"oldLines":8,"newStart":37,"newLines":8,"lines":["     mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional","         Determines the output size:","         - 'valid': output size is ``len(a) - window_size + 1`` (default)","-        - 'same': output size is ``len(a)`` (padded to match input)","-        - 'full': output size is ``len(a) + window_size - 1`` (padded on both sides)","+        - 'same': output size is ``len(a)`` (centered windows within bounds)","+        - 'full': output size is ``len(a) + window_size - 1`` (all window positions)"," ","     Returns","     -------"]},{"oldStart":118,"oldLines":29,"newStart":118,"newLines":8,"lines":["     output_shape[axis] = output_size","     result = np.empty(output_shape, dtype=np.float64)"," ","-    # It has been tested on Linux and macOS, and\nwith Python 3.10-3.12. There is one CI job to keep the build stable. This may\nhave rough edges, please open an issue if you run into a problem._\n\n### Developer build\n\n**Install build tools:** Use one of:\n\n- `mamba env create -f environment.yml && mamba activate numpy-dev`\n\n- `python -m pip install -r requirements/build_requirements.txt`\n  *Note: also make sure you have `pkg-config` and the usual system dependencies\n  for NumPy*\n\nThen install spin:\n- `python -m pip install spin`\n\n**Compile and install:** `spin build`\n\nThis builds in the `build/` directory, and installs into the `build-install` directory.\n\nThen run the test suite or a shell via `spin`:\n```\nspin test\nspin ipython\n```\n\nAlternatively, to use the package, add it to your `PYTHONPATH`:\n```\nexport PYTHONPATH=${PWD}/build/lib64/python3.10/site-packages  # may vary\npytest --pyargs numpy\n```\n\n\n### pip install\n\nNote that `pip` will use the default build system, which is now Meson.\nCommands such as `pip install .` or `pip install --no-build-isolation .`\nwill work as expected, as does building an sdist or wheel with `python -m build`,\nor `pip install -e . --no-build-isolation` for an editable install.\nFor a more complete developer experience than editable installs, consider using\n`spin` instead though (see above).\n\n\n### Workaround for a hiccup on Fedora\n\n- Fedora does not distribute `openblas.pc`. Install the following file in `~/lib/pkgconfig/openblas.pc`:\n\n```\nprefix=/usr\nincludedir=${prefix}/include\nlibdir=${prefix}/lib64\n\nName: openblas\nDescription: OpenBLAS is an optimized BLAS library based on GotoBLAS2 1.13 BSD version\nVersion: 0.3.19\nCflags: -I${includedir}/openblas\nLibs: -L${libdir} -lopenblas\n```\n\nThen build with:\n\n```\nspin build -- -Dpkg_config_path=${HOME}/lib/pkgconfig\n```\n","numLines":68,"startLine":1,"totalLines":68}}}

Linear Algebra, Fourier Transforms, Random Number Generation\n     9→\n    10→How to use the documentation\n    11→----------------------------\n    12→Documentation is available in two forms: docstrings provided\n    13→with the code, and a loose standing reference guide, available from\n    14→`the NumPy homepage <https://numpy.org>`_.\n    15→\n    16→We recommend exploring the docstrings using\n    17→`IPython <https://ipython.org>`_, an advanced Python shell with\n    18→TAB-completion and introspection capabilities.  See below for further\n    19→instructions.\n    20→\n    21→The docstring examples assume that `numpy` has been imported as ``np``::\n    22→\n    23→  >>> import numpy as np\n    24→\n    25→Code snippets are indicated by three greater-than signs::\n    26→\n    27→  >>> x = 42\n    28→  >>> x = x + 1\n    29→\n    30→Use the built-in ``help`` function to view a function's docstring::\n    31→\n    32→  >>> help(np.sort)\n    33→  ... # doctest: +SKIP\n    34→\n    35→For some objects, ``np.info(obj)`` may provide additional help. The key is recognizing that each output position's window is defined by these input index boundaries, accounting for clipping at the edges.\n\nI can express this with a formula: start_idx = max(0, i - window_size + 1) and end_idx = min(axis_size, i + 1).
